25:T1c06,<entryFree id="n27693" key="ظَنَّ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <itype>1</itype>        
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">ظَنَّ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form>, aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bu" lang="ar" marker="Zanu3a">ظَنُنَ</orth>
                  </form>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">ظَنٌّ</foreign>, (Msb,) [<hi rend="ital">He thought, opined, supposed,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">conjectured:</hi> and <hi rend="ital">he doubted:</hi> and <hi rend="ital">he knew,</hi> but <hi rend="ital">not by ocular perception:</hi> see <foreign lang="ar">ظَنٌّ</foreign> below:] you say, <foreign lang="ar">ظَنَنْتُ الشَّىْءَ</foreign>, aor. <foreign lang="ar">أَظُنُّهُ</foreign>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">ظَنٌّ</foreign>; and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n27693-1" target="اِظَّنَنْتُهُ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">اِظْطَنَنْتُهُ</foreign>; and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n27693-2" target="تَظَنَّنْتُهُ" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">تَظَنَّيْتُهُ</foreign>, this last formed by changing the last <foreign lang="ar">ن</foreign> into <foreign lang="ar">ى</foreign>: [i. e. <hi rend="ital">I thought the thing,</hi> &amp;c:] and Lh mentions, as heard from the Benoo-Suleym, <foreign lang="ar">ظَنْتُ ذَاكَ</foreign> i. e. <foreign lang="ar">ظَنَنْتُ ذاك</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I thought that,</hi> &amp;c.] like <foreign lang="ar">ظَلْتُ</foreign> and other instances of the dial. of Suleym. (M.) [In the first of the senses expl. above, it governs two objective complements, which are originally an inchoative and an enunciative:] you say, <foreign lang="ar">ظَنَنْتُكَ زَيْدًا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I thought thee Zeyd,</hi> originally <hi rend="ital">I thought thou wast Zeyd</hi>], and <foreign lang="ar">ظَنَنْتُ زَيْدًا إِيَّاكَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I thought Zeyd thee,</hi> originally <hi rend="ital">I thought Zeyd was thou</hi>], denoting by a pronoun what is originally an inchoative [in the former phrase] and what is originally an enunciative [in the latter phrase]. (S, TA.) It is also used [in this sense] in the same manner as a verb signifying an oath, the Arabs giving it the same kind of complement, saying, <foreign lang="ar">ظَنَنْتُ لَعَبْدُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">ٱللّٰهِ خَيْرٌ مِنْكَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I thought surely 'Abd-Allah was better than thou</hi>]. (S in art. <foreign lang="ar">درد</foreign>.) [<foreign lang="ar">ظَنَّ بِهِ كَذَا</foreign> means <hi rend="ital">I thought of him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it, such a thing:</hi> and <hi rend="ital">I thought such a thing to be in him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it:</hi> and is used in relation to good and to evil.] It is said in the Kur [xxxiii. 10], <foreign lang="ar">وَتَطُنُّونَ بِٱللّٰهِ ٱلظُّنُونَا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">And ye were thinking, of God,</hi> various <hi rend="ital">thoughts</hi>]. (M.) Accord. to Sb, <foreign lang="ar">ظَنَنْتُ بِهِ</foreign> means <hi rend="ital">I made him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it, the place</hi> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">object</hi>] <hi rend="ital">of my</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">ظَنّ</foreign> [or <hi rend="ital">thought,</hi> &amp;c.]. (M.) [In all these exs. the verb denotes a state of mind between doubt and certainty, but the latter is predominant: and hence <foreign lang="ar">ظَنَّ</foreign> sometimes means <hi rend="ital">He doubted:</hi> and sometimes, <hi rend="ital">he knew, by considering with endeavour to understand, not by ocular perception;</hi> being more frequently used in this sense than as meaning “ he doubted, ” though not so frequently as it is in the sense of “ he thought, ” whence the meaning “ he knew ” is held by some to be tropical.] <foreign lang="ar">إِنَّى</foreign>, <foreign lang="ar">ظَنَنْتُ أَنِّى مُلَاقٍ حِسَابِيَهْ</foreign>, in the Kur [lxix. 20], means <hi rend="ital">Verily I knew</hi> [<hi rend="ital">that I should meet with my reckoning</hi>]. (T.) And <foreign lang="ar">ٱلَّذِينَ يَظُنُّونَ أَنَّهُمْ مُلَاقُو</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">رَبِّهِمْ</foreign>, in the same [ii. 43], means <hi rend="ital">Who know</hi> [<hi rend="ital">that they shall meet their Lord,</hi> lit., <hi rend="ital">be meeters of their Lord</hi>]. (Msb.) And <foreign lang="ar">ظَنَنْتُ مَا قَالَ</foreign>, occurring in a trad., means <hi rend="ital">I knew</hi> [<hi rend="ital">what he meant to say</hi> by his making a sign with his hand]. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">ظَنَنْتُهُ</foreign>, (M, Mgh, Msb,) aor. as above, (Msb,) and so the inf. n., (M,) signifies also <hi rend="ital">I suspected him; thought evil of him;</hi> (M, Mgh, Msb;) and (M) so   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n27693-3" target="اِظَّنَنْتُهُ" n="3" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> (S, M, Mgh, K) and <foreign lang="ar">اِظْطَنَنْتُهُ</foreign> (M, TA) and <foreign lang="ar">اِطَّنَنْتُهُ</foreign>. (TA.) [Thus, too,   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n27693-4" target="أَظْنَنْتُهُ" n="4" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> accord. to several copies of the S and accord. to the CK; but this is app. a mistranscription.] In the saying of Ibn-Seereen, <foreign lang="ar">لَمْ يَكُنْ عَلِىٌّ <ref cref="n27693-5" target="يُظَّنُّ" n="5" type="6" subtype="FTFSO" lang="ar"/> فِى قَتْلِ عُثْمَانَ</foreign>, (T, S, K, but in the T <foreign lang="ar">مَا كَان</foreign>,) meaning <hi rend="ital">Alee was not suspected</hi> [<hi rend="ital">in the case of the slaying of 'Othmán</hi>], (T,) <foreign lang="ar">يُظَّنُّ</foreign> is of the measure <foreign lang="ar">يُفْتَعَلُ</foreign>, originally <foreign lang="ar">يُظْتَنُّ</foreign>: (T, S, K:) so says A'Obeyd: (T:) or, as some relate it, the word is <foreign lang="ar">يُطَّنُّ</foreign>. (TA.) One says, <foreign lang="ar">هُوَ <ref cref="n27693-6" target="يُظَّنُّ" n="6" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>بِكَذَا</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">يُطَّنُّ</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">He is suspected of such a thing.</hi> (TA in art. <foreign lang="ar">طن</foreign>.) And <foreign lang="ar">طَنَنْتُ بِزَيْدٍ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">ظَنَنْتُ زَيْدًا</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">I suspected Zeyd:</hi> in <pb n="1925"/> this sense the verb has a single objective complement. (TA.)    </entryFree>26:T45c,<entryFree id="n27695" key="التَّظَنِّى" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <itype>5</itype>        
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">التَّظَنِّى</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form> means <hi rend="ital">The exercising, employing,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">using, of</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الظَّنّ</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">thought,</hi> &amp;c.]; originally <foreign lang="ar">التَّظَنُّنُ</foreign>. (S, K.) A'Obeyd says, <foreign lang="ar">تَظَنَّيْتُ</foreign> is from <foreign lang="ar">ظَنَنْتُ</foreign>, and is originally <foreign lang="ar">تَظَنَّنْتُ</foreign>; the <foreign lang="ar">ن</foreign> being many, one of them is changed into <foreign lang="ar">ى</foreign>: it is like <foreign lang="ar">قَصَّيْتُ</foreign>, which is originally <foreign lang="ar">قَصَّصْتُ</foreign>. (T.)       <sense type="A" n="2">-A2-</sense>  See also 1, first sentence.    </entryFree>27:Tbad,<entryFree id="n27696" key="ظَنٌّ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">ظَنٌّ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form> is a simple subst. as well as an inf. n.; (TA;) and signifies <hi rend="ital">Thought, opinion, supposition,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">conjecture:</hi> (Er-Rághib, Mgh, TA:) or <hi rend="ital">a preponderant belief, with the admission that the contrary may be the case:</hi> (KT, El-Munáwee, TA:) or <hi rend="ital">a preponderating wavering between the two extremes in indecisive belief:</hi> (K:) or <hi rend="ital">an inference from a sign,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">mark,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">token; when strong, leading to knowledge; and when weak, not exceeding the limit of</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">وَهْم</foreign>: (Er-Rághib, TA:) or <hi rend="ital">doubt</hi> or <hi rend="ital">uncertainty;</hi> (T, M;) or it has this meaning also; (Er-Rághib, TA;) <hi rend="ital">contr. of</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">يَقِينٌ</foreign>: (Msb:) and sometimes it is put in the place, (S, K,) or used in the sense, (Mgh, Msb,) of <foreign lang="ar">عِلْمٌ</foreign>, (S, Mgh, K,) or <foreign lang="ar">يَقِينٌ</foreign>, (Msb,) [i. e. <hi rend="ital">knowledge,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">certainty,</hi>] in which sense it is [held by some to be] tropical; (Mgh;) or it signifies also <hi rend="ital">knowledge,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">certainty,</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">يَقِينٌ</foreign>, T, M,) <hi rend="ital">such as is obtained by considering with endeavour to understand, not by ocular perception,</hi> (M,) or <hi rend="ital">not such as relates to an object of sense:</hi> (MF:) and it also means <hi rend="ital">suspicion,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">evil opinion:</hi> (Er-Rághib, TA: [but in this last sense, <foreign lang="ar">ظِنَّةٌ</foreign> is more common:]) as a subst., (TA,) its pl. is <foreign lang="ar">ظُنُونٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">أَظَانِينُ</foreign>, (M, K, TA,) the latter anomalous, or (as ISd says, TA) it may be pl. of   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n27696-1" target="أُظْنُونَةٌ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n27705"/></foreign>, but this I do not know. (M, TA.) One says, <foreign lang="ar">هُوَ سَيِّئُ الظَّنِّ بِكُلِّ أَحَدٍ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He is evil in opinion of everyone</hi>]. (M.) [And <foreign lang="ar">سَآءَ ظَنُّهُ بِفُلَانٍ</foreign>

(M, Mgh, Msb, TA.) One says, <foreign lang="ar">مَوْضِعُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">كَذَا مَظِنَّةٌ مِنْ فُلَانٍ</foreign> i. e. <hi rend="ital">Such a place is a place in which such a one is known</hi> [&amp;c.] <hi rend="ital">to be.</hi> (S, TA.)
